        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

        }

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





When using the chrome.debugger API, one of the methods an extension can call is Page.captureScreenshot. That method allows a screenshot of the frame being debugged to be captured.



<span class="line"><!---->When using the chrome.debugger API, one of the methods an extension can call is Page.captureScreenshot. That method allows a screenshot of the frame being debugged to be captured.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When the fromSurface parameter passed to that method is set to false, the screenshot is captured from the view, rather than the surface. One consequence of that is that any content drawn on top of the debugged frame will be captured in the screenshot.



<span class="line"><!---->When the fromSurface parameter passed to that method is set to false, the screenshot is captured from the view, rather than the surface. One consequence of that is that any content drawn on top of the debugged frame will be captured in the screenshot.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





An extension can use that fact to capture the contents of local files.



<span class="line"><!---->An extension can use that fact to capture the contents of local files.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





Chrome Version: Tested on 84.0.4147.125 (stable) and 86.0.4233.0 (canary)



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: Tested on 84.0.4147.125 (stable) and 86.0.4233.0 (canary)<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Windows 10, version 1909



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Windows 10, version 1909<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





1. Install the attached extension. Ensure that "Allow access to file URLs" isn't checked.



<span class="line"><!---->1. Install the attached extension. Ensure that "Allow access to file URLs" isn't checked.<!----></span>



<br>





2. Once installed, the extension will download local_file.html.



<span class="line"><!---->2. Once installed, the extension will download local_file.html.<!----></span>



<br>





3. Once the download has completed, the extension will open local_file.html in a new tab.



<span class="line"><!---->3. Once the download has completed, the extension will open local_file.html in a new tab.<!----></span>



<br>





4. local_file.html contains two subframes: one that loads file:///c:/ and another that loads iframe.html from within the extension. Because the second frame has an absolute position, it will be drawn underneath the first frame.



<span class="line"><!---->4. local_file.html contains two subframes: one that loads file:///c:/ and another that loads iframe.html from within the extension. Because the second frame has an absolute position, it will be drawn underneath the first frame.<!----></span>



<br>





5. The extension will then attach the debugger to iframe.html and call Page.captureScreenshot with fromSurface set to false.



<span class="line"><!---->5. The extension will then attach the debugger to iframe.html and call Page.captureScreenshot with fromSurface set to false.<!----></span>



<br>





6. Once the extension has received the screenshot data, it will make the following call:



<span class="line"><!---->6. Once the extension has received the screenshot data, it will make the following call:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





chrome.tabs.create({url: "data:image/png;base64," + screenshotData});



<span class="line"><!---->chrome.tabs.create({url: "data:image/png;base64," + screenshotData});<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The resulting tab should show that the contents of the file:///c:/ frame have been captured. This is true even though the file:///c:/ frame is a sibling of the captured frame and not contained within it.



<span class="line"><!---->The resulting tab should show that the contents of the file:///c:/ frame have been captured. This is true even though the file:///c:/ frame is a sibling of the captured frame and not contained within it.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This issue is similar to 



<span class="line"><!---->This issue is similar to <!----></span>





issue 1116444



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1116444" title="Security: Extensions can capture contents of local files using Page.captureScreenshot"><!---->issue 1116444<!----></a>





, 



<span class="line"><!---->, <!----></span>





which also uses Page.captureScreenshot.



<span class="line"><!---->which also uses Page.captureScreenshot.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

I don't think this issue is a duplicate. While the original demonstration extension does now fail because it's attempting to call Page.captureScreenshot for a nested frame, it's simple enough to adjust the extension so that it calls Page.captureScreenshot on a top-level frame, but still captures the contents of a local file.



<span class="line"><!---->I don't think this issue is a duplicate. While the original demonstration extension does now fail because it's attempting to call Page.captureScreenshot for a nested frame, it's simple enough to adjust the extension so that it calls Page.captureScreenshot on a top-level frame, but still captures the contents of a local file.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I've attached an updated extension here that demonstrates that. To test:



<span class="line"><!---->I've attached an updated extension here that demonstrates that. To test:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. Install the attached extension. Ensure that "Allow access to file URLs" isn't checked.



<span class="line"><!---->1. Install the attached extension. Ensure that "Allow access to file URLs" isn't checked.<!----></span>



<br>





2. Once installed, the extension will open two new tabs: one containing manifest.json and one containing file:///c:/.



<span class="line"><!---->2. Once installed, the extension will open two new tabs: one containing manifest.json and one containing file:///c:/.<!----></span>



<br>





3. The extension will then attach the debugger to the manifest.json tab and call Page.captureScreenshot with fromSurface set to false.



<span class="line"><!---->3. The extension will then attach the debugger to the manifest.json tab and call Page.captureScreenshot with fromSurface set to false.<!----></span>



<br>





4. Immediately after making that call, the extension will mark the file:///c:/ tab as active.



<span class="line"><!---->4. Immediately after making that call, the extension will mark the file:///c:/ tab as active.<!----></span>



<br>





5. Once the extension has received the screenshot data, it will make the following call:



<span class="line"><!---->5. Once the extension has received the screenshot data, it will make the following call:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





chrome.tabs.create({url: "data:image/png;base64," + screenshotData});



<span class="line"><!---->chrome.tabs.create({url: "data:image/png;base64," + screenshotData});<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The resulting tab should show that the contents of the file:///c:/ tab have been captured (along with the rest of the browser window). This is true even though the extension isn't attached to the file:///c:/ tab.



<span class="line"><!---->The resulting tab should show that the contents of the file:///c:/ tab have been captured (along with the rest of the browser window). This is true even though the extension isn't attached to the file:///c:/ tab.<!----></span>

I think the specific reason the behavior described in the previous comment occurs is because there's a delay (of 1/6th of a second) when capturing a screenshot from the view:



<span class="line"><!---->I think the specific reason the behavior described in the previous comment occurs is because there's a delay (of 1/6th of a second) when capturing a screenshot from the view:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:content/browser/renderer_host/render_widget_host_impl.cc;l=3356;drc=279d90cbebb0be2bff181c693e6c06cb4ac0f3e8



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:content/browser/renderer_host/render_widget_host_impl.cc;l=3356;drc=279d90cbebb0be2bff181c693e6c06cb4ac0f3e8"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/master:content/browser/renderer_host/render_widget_host_impl.cc;l=3356;drc=279d90cbebb0be2bff181c693e6c06cb4ac0f3e8<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





During that delay, if another tab is made active, the screenshot will ultimately show the contents of that tab, rather than the tab being debugged.



<span class="line"><!---->During that delay, if another tab is made active, the screenshot will ultimately show the contents of that tab, rather than the tab being debugged.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I think the fact that the screenshot is captured from the OS-level window is also part of it, since it means that whatever is shown within that window at the time is what will be captured, regardless of whether that's the original tab or another tab.



<span class="line"><!---->I think the fact that the screenshot is captured from the OS-level window is also part of it, since it means that whatever is shown within that window at the time is what will be captured, regardless of whether that's the original tab or another tab.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.
